## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) — nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, matching second-order ODE models for (nonlinear) harmonic oscillators with restoring forces, damping, and possible external/parametric forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (small-amplitude oscillator with linear stiffness and viscous damping; signs typically restoring/dissipative)
- Conservative force from potential (generic): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (restoring force as odd polynomial; softening/stiffening springs)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven/damped): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity with linear damping)
- Purely nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (damping grows with speed, e.g., fluid-like drag; linear stiffness)
- Coulomb (dry) friction term: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (smoothed sign(v) friction using available v only)
- Van der Pol oscillator (in x–v form): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x| leading to limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excited oscillations via velocity-dependent damping)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (periodic restoring torque; reduces to linear for small x)
- Driven oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (bistability/chaos under forcing)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type behavior/parametric resonance)
- State-dependent frequency (amplitude-dependent stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2) * x - c2 * v (effective frequency increases/decreases with amplitude)
- Energy-based form with nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (damping changes with displacement, e.g., geometric effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (and is approximately an odd function of x), with minimal direct dependence on v except damping.
- Viscous damping signature: terms proportional to v reduce oscillation amplitude; nonlinear damping often appears as v*Abs(v) or v**3 to model speed-amplified dissipation.
- Hardening vs softening spring: a positive cubic stiffness term in the restoring force (e.g., -c * x**3) tends to harden (frequency increases with amplitude), while the opposite sign softens.
- Self-excited limit cycles: factors like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- Pendulum/rotational periodicity: sin(c*x) restoring terms imply periodic phase-space structure and non-polynomial restoring torque.
- External periodic forcing: additive cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms produce entrainment, resonance peaks, and possible quasiperiodicity/chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric resonance indicator: time-multiplication of x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) suggests instability tongues typical of Mathieu-like systems.
- Symmetry checks: many mechanical oscillators are invariant under (x,v) -> (-x,-v), encouraging dv_dt forms that are odd in x and odd in v for damping components.
